<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> was long-planned;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RDS_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-RDS-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> had approached series creator Stephen Hillenburg for a film based on the show, but he refused for more than a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edel1-6">[6]</a></sup> Hillenburg was concerned, after watching <i><a href="/wiki/The_Iron_Giant" title="The Iron Giant">The Iron Giant</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">Toy Story</a></i> with his sons, about the challenge of SpongeBob and Patrick doing something more cinematically-consequential and inspiring without losing what he calls the SpongeBob "cadence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edel1-6">[6]</a></sup> He said, on a break from season-four post-production, "To do a 75-minute movie about SpongeBob wanting to make some jellyfish jelly would be a mistake, I think [...] This had to be SpongeBob in a great adventure. That's where the comedy's coming from, having these two naïve characters, SpongeBob and Patrick, a doofus and an idiot, on this incredibly dangerous heroic odyssey with all the odds against them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel1_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Edel1-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<table cellspacing="5" class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 2em; font-size: 85%; background:#c6dbf7; color:black; width:28em; max-width: 40%;">
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">I never wanted to do a movie because I didn't think that what we wanted to say needed to be in a movie. I like the short form for animation. Then this story idea came up that lent itself to a longer format. You can't do a road trip adventure in a short form.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">— <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hillenburg" title="Stephen Hillenburg">Stephen Hillenburg</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 2002, Hillenburg and the show's staff stopped making episodes to work on the film after the show's third season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> The film's plot originally had SpongeBob rescue Patrick from a fisherman in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> an obvious reference to the 2003 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i>, this was later said by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kenny" title="Tom Kenny">Tom Kenny</a> (the voice of SpongeBob) to be a "joke" plot to keep fans busy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> Hillenburg wrote the film with five other writer-animators from the show (<a href="/wiki/Paul_Tibbitt" title="Paul Tibbitt">Paul Tibbitt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Drymon" title="Derek Drymon">Derek Drymon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Springer" title="Aaron Springer">Aaron Springer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent_Osborne" title="Kent Osborne">Kent Osborne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hill_(director)" title="Tim Hill (director)">Tim Hill</a>) over a three-month period in a room of a former <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_California" title="Glendale, California">Glendale, California</a> bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel1_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Edel1-6">[6]</a></sup> Osborne said, "It was hugely fun [...] although it did get kind of gamy in there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel1_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Edel1-6">[6]</a></sup> At the beginning of the series, Hillenburg screened a number of silent shorts (from <a href="/wiki/Laurel_and_Hardy" title="Laurel and Hardy">Laurel and Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buster_Keaton" title="Buster Keaton">Buster Keaton</a>) and work by two modern comic actors: <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lewis" title="Jerry Lewis">Jerry Lewis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pee-wee_Herman" title="Pee-wee Herman">Pee-wee Herman</a>, both obvious inspirations for SpongeBob.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> For the film, the writers created a mythical hero's quest: the search for a stolen crown, which brings SpongeBob and Patrick to the surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fagerbakke" title="Bill Fagerbakke">Bill Fagerbakke</a> (the voice of Patrick) said about the plot, "It's just nuts. I'm continually dazzled and delighted with what these guys came up with."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbsorbingTales_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-AbsorbingTales-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the film was completed, Hillenburg wanted to <a href="/wiki/Series_finale" title="Series finale">end the series</a> "so [it] wouldn't <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jump_the_shark" title="Jump the shark">jump the shark</a>". However, Nickelodeon desired more episodes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> Hillenburg stated: "Well, there was concern when we did the movie [in 2004] that the show had peaked. There were concerns among executives at Nickelodeon."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> As a result, Hillenburg resigned as the series' <a href="/wiki/Showrunner" title="Showrunner">showrunner</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huffington_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huffington-13">[13]</a></sup> appointing supervising producer, writer, director, and <a href="/wiki/Storyboard_artist" title="Storyboard artist">storyboard artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tibbitt" title="Paul Tibbitt">Paul Tibbitt</a> to succeed him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tibbitt_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tibbitt-14">[14]</a></sup> Tibbitt was one of Hillenburg's favorite crew members:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> "[I] totally trusted him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Childhood_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Childhood-16">[16]</a></sup> Tibbitt would remain showrunner until he was succeeded in 2015 by the show's creative director Vincent Waller and staff writer Marc Ceccarelli. He has also acted as an executive producer since 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tibbitt_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tibbitt-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Hillenburg no longer writes or runs the show on a day-to-day basis, but reviews each episode and submitted suggestions: "I figure when I'm pretty old I can still paint [...] I don't know about running shows."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huffington_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Huffington-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kenny" title="Tom Kenny">Tom Kenny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fagerbakke" title="Bill Fagerbakke">Bill Fagerbakke</a> and the crew confirmed that they had completed four episodes for broadcast on Nickelodeon in early 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets2_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets2-20">[20]</a></sup> and planned to finish a total of about 20 for the fourth season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets1_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets2_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets2-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2015, Hillenburg returned to the show following the completion of the <a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_Movie:_Sponge_Out_of_Water" title="The SpongeBob Movie: Sponge Out of Water">second movie</a> as an executive producer, now having greater creative input and attending crew meetings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2003, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Engel" title="Jules Engel">Jules Engel</a>, Hillenburg's mentor when he studied experimental animation at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_the_Arts" title="California Institute of the Arts">California Institute of the Arts</a>, died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Hillenburg dedicated the film to him: "He truly was the most influential artistic person in my life. I consider him my 'Art Dad.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thoughts_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thoughts-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animation">Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were a number of stages involved in the making of the film, beginning with a rough animation process of ideas drawn on <a href="/wiki/Post-it_note" title="Post-it note">Post-it notes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InsidePineapple_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-InsidePineapple-27">[27]</a></sup> The writers drew, working from rough outlines rather than scripts (which made the humor more visual than verbal).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> Hillenburg said, "It's in the characters' extreme body language, in how they slither capriciously around the deadpan frames."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> The storyboard artists, including <a href="/wiki/Sherm_Cohen" title="Sherm Cohen">Sherm Cohen</a>, then illustrated ideas conceived by the writers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbsorbingTales_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-AbsorbingTales-9">[9]</a></sup> In the series <a href="/wiki/Tom_Yasumi" title="Tom Yasumi">Tom Yasumi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Overtoom" title="Andrew Overtoom">Andrew Overtoom</a> do the <a href="/wiki/Storyboard#Animatics" title="Storyboard">animatics</a>, but director Hillenburg and writer <a href="/wiki/Derek_Drymon" title="Derek Drymon">Derek Drymon</a> did the animatics for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overtoom_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overtoom-28">[28]</a></sup> Yasumi and Overtoom were the film's animation-timing directors, concentrating on the sheets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overtoom_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overtoom-28">[28]</a></sup> <i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> was animated at <a href="/wiki/Rough_Draft_Studios" title="Rough Draft Studios">Rough Draft Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RDS_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-RDS-5">[5]</a></sup> The animators worked semi-digitally; pencil-drawn poses would be <a href="/wiki/Compositing" title="Compositing">composited</a> into layouts in <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop" title="Adobe Photoshop">Photoshop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Series writer and storyboard artist <a href="/wiki/Erik_Wiese" title="Erik Wiese">Erik Wiese</a> left the show for a year to work on <i><a href="/wiki/Samurai_Jack" title="Samurai Jack">Samurai Jack</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Danny_Phantom" title="Danny Phantom">Danny Phantom</a></i>, but returned to do storyboards and character layout for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> He "always wanted to be a feature animator, and the movie felt like I was on the character animation end", describing the experience as "a blast—it felt like coming home."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hillenburg enjoyed the process of making the film:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> "The TV schedule is tight, and you don't always have a lot of time to work on your drawings."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> He appreciated the film's <a href="/wiki/Traditional_animation" title="Traditional animation">hand-drawn animation</a>: "I think the movie's drawings are much superior than the TV show", although <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">CGI animation</a> was flourishing at the time of the film's release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> "There's a lot of talk about 2-D being dead, and I hope people don't think that. Even <a href="/wiki/Brad_Bird" title="Brad Bird">Brad Bird</a> is a proponent of 2-D. He would agree with me that it's all about what you're trying to say. There are many ways to tell a story, and what's unique about animation is that there are many styles with which to tell a story."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-7"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Clay_animation" title="Clay animation">clay animation</a> scenes were shot by Mark Caballero, Seamus Walsh and Chris Finnegan at <a href="/wiki/Screen_Novelties" title="Screen Novelties">Screen Novelties</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thoughts_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thoughts-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film features live-action scenes directed by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Osborne_(filmmaker)" title="Mark Osborne (filmmaker)">Mark Osborne</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbsorbingTales_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-AbsorbingTales-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Replica1_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Replica1-30">[30]</a></sup> The ship used during the 30-second opening featuring the pirates singing the theme was the <a href="/wiki/Bounty_(1960_ship)" title="Bounty (1960 ship)"><i>Bounty</i></a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bounty1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bounty1-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> a 180-foot (55 m)-long, enlarged reconstruction of the 1787 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> sailing ship <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bounty" title="HMS Bounty">HMS <i>Bounty</i></a> built for 1962's <i><a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty_(1962_film)" title="Mutiny on the Bounty (1962 film)">Mutiny on the Bounty</a></i>. The ship has appeared in a number of other films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Treasure_Island_(1999_film)" title="Treasure Island (1999 film)">Treasure Island</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest</a></i> (2006) and <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i> (2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Trailer_(promotion)" title="Trailer (promotion)">film trailers</a>, live-action scenes were taken from <i><a href="/wiki/Das_Boot" title="Das Boot">Das Boot</a></i> (1981), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunt_for_Red_October_(film)" title="The Hunt for Red October (film)">The Hunt for Red October</a></i> (1990) and <i><a href="/wiki/U-571_(film)" title="U-571 (film)">U-571</a></i> (2000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_7-8"><a href="#cite_note-EVT-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg"><img alt="Man working on oversized replica of a smiling man" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="470" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg/240px-David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg/360px-David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f5/David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Hasselhoff_replica_for_The_SpongeBob_Movie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The crew built an oversized replica of David Hasselhoff for visual effect.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_(1982_TV_series)" title="Knight Rider (1982 TV series)">Knight Rider</a></i> actor <a href="/wiki/David_Hasselhoff" title="David Hasselhoff">David Hasselhoff</a> made a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo</a> in the live-action scenes, offering SpongeBob and Patrick a ride to Bikini Bottom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS1_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAS1-35">[35]</a></sup> The scene was originally written before consulting Hasselhoff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets1_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets2_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets2-20">[20]</a></sup> Hillenburg was pleased with the storyboards;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> Lead storyboard artist <a href="/wiki/Sherm_Cohen" title="Sherm Cohen">Sherm Cohen</a> said, "He had been wrestling with the ending for quite a while, and finally he was ready to pitch his ideas to some of the other board artists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> Hillenburg was counting on casting Hasselhoff, and the first question asked him was "So, do we have Hasselhoff?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> He replied "No", with a grin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-6"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> Hasselhoff eventually agreed, before seeing the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets1_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets2_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets2-20">[20]</a></sup> Hillenburg said about the actor, "He's a great guy [...] He was great at making fun of himself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets1_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10Secrets2_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-10Secrets2-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The crew built a 750-pound (340 kg), 12-foot (3.7 m) replica of Hasselhoff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Replica1_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Replica1-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS1_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-LAS1-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The $100,000 replica was kept at Hasselhoff's home;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS2_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAS2-37">[37]</a></sup> he has said, "It freaked me out because it was so lifelike, with teeth, when you touch it [it] feels like real skin. It's soft, like your skin."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS2_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-LAS2-37">[37]</a></sup> At the completion of filming, Hasselhoff said, "That's ridiculously awesome. What are you gonna do with it?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS2_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-LAS2-37">[37]</a></sup> Asked by the crew if he wanted to keep it, he answered, "Uh, yeah. Okay."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS2_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-LAS2-37">[37]</a></sup> Hasselhoff filmed in cold water, where he was pulled by a sled nine yards across the sea;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AbsorbingTales_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-AbsorbingTales-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAS1_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-LAS1-35">[35]</a></sup> he described the experience as "cold but [a] lot of fun."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InsidePineapple_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-InsidePineapple-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late March 2014, Hasselhoff auctioned off the replica with other memorabilia collected during his career. <a href="/wiki/Julien%27s_Auctions" title="Julien's Auctions">Julien's Auctions</a> handled the item's sale, which were expected to bring in between $20,000 and $30,000. The auction was scheduled to begin on April 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast_2">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_SpongeBob_SquarePants_characters" title="List of SpongeBob SquarePants characters">List of SpongeBob SquarePants characters</a></div>
<p>The film stars the series' main cast members, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kenny" title="Tom Kenny">Tom Kenny</a> as <a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants_(character)" title="SpongeBob SquarePants (character)">SpongeBob SquarePants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fagerbakke" title="Bill Fagerbakke">Bill Fagerbakke</a> as <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Star" title="Patrick Star">Patrick Star</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodger_Bumpass" title="Rodger Bumpass">Rodger Bumpass</a> as <a href="/wiki/Squidward_Tentacles" title="Squidward Tentacles">Squidward Tentacles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clancy_Brown" title="Clancy Brown">Clancy Brown</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mr._Krabs" title="Mr. Krabs">Mr. Krabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Lawrence" title="Carolyn Lawrence">Carolyn Lawrence</a> as <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Cheeks" title="Sandy Cheeks">Sandy Cheeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mr._Lawrence" title="Mr. Lawrence">Mr. Lawrence</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plankton_(SpongeBob_SquarePants)" title="Plankton (SpongeBob SquarePants)">Plankton</a>. It also features <a href="/wiki/Jill_Talley" title="Jill Talley">Jill Talley</a> as Karen, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jo_Catlett" title="Mary Jo Catlett">Mary Jo Catlett</a> as Mrs. Puff, <a href="/wiki/Lori_Alan" title="Lori Alan">Lori Alan</a> as Pearl, <a href="/wiki/Dee_Bradley_Baker" title="Dee Bradley Baker">Dee Bradley Baker</a> as Perch Perkins, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alazraqui" title="Carlos Alazraqui">Carlos Alazraqui</a> as king Neptune's squire, Aaron Hendry as the <a href="/wiki/Cyclops" title="Cyclops">Cyclops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Ross" title="Neil Ross">Neil Ross</a> as the voice of the <a href="/wiki/Cyclops" title="Cyclops">Cyclops</a>. In addition to the series' cast, it was reported on March 23, 2004 that <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Tambor" title="Jeffrey Tambor">Jeffrey Tambor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alec_Baldwin" title="Alec Baldwin">Alec Baldwin</a> would play new characters princess Mindy, King Neptune and Dennis, respectively, and <a href="/wiki/David_Hasselhoff" title="David Hasselhoff">David Hasselhoff</a> would appear as himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cast1_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cast1-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Johansson accepted the role because she likes cartoons and was a fan of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ren_%26_Stimpy_Show" title="The Ren &amp; Stimpy Show">The Ren &amp; Stimpy Show</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-SW-42">[42]</a></sup> When Jeffrey Tambor signed for his voice cameo, he saw his character (King Neptune) and joked, "This is me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-SW-42">[42]</a></sup> He remembered the first cartoon he saw, <i><a href="/wiki/Bambi" title="Bambi">Bambi</a></i>: "My first cartoon, I had to be carried out crying [...] It was <i>Bambi</i>. It's like the great American wound: the death of Bambi's mother. 'Run, Bambi, run!'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Another guest voice was Alec Baldwin;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cast1_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cast1-41">[41]</a></sup> Stephen Hillenburg said that the actor recorded his character Dennis on a "phone":<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-SW-42">[42]</a></sup> "I wouldn't say that about his performance. He might be mad if we said that. Technically, it was like he was in another booth in the studio."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-SW-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Baywatch</i> and <i>Knight Rider</i> star David Hasselhoff accepted the role when his daughters, Taylor-Ann and <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Hasselhoff" title="Hayley Hasselhoff">Hayley</a>, urged him:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasselhoff2_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hasselhoff2-44">[44]</a></sup> "I got an offer to do a cameo in the <i>SpongeBob Movie</i> and I turned to my girls, who were like 16 and 14, and I said, 'Who's SpongeBob?' and they said, 'Oh my God, Dad, it's the number one cartoon in the world, you gotta do it.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasselhoff2_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hasselhoff2-44">[44]</a></sup> Hasselhoff enjoyed his cameo: "It was great fun and to this day around the world kids stop me and say, 'Are you David Hasselhoff?' because I was the only human in the picture."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasselhoff2_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hasselhoff2-44">[44]</a></sup> Hasselhoff said that the film gained him new fans: "It's amazing - so many of the kids were so young and didn't see <i>Baywatch</i> and <i>Knight Rider</i> so I got a whole new legion of fans."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hasselhoff2_44-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hasselhoff2-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie_%E2%80%93_Music_from_the_Movie_and_More..." title="The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie – Music from the Movie and More...">The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie – Music from the Movie and More...</a> and <a href="/wiki/Best_Day_Ever" title="Best Day Ever">Best Day Ever</a></div>
<p>Gregor Narholz composed the score for the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> conducting the recording sessions (in 5.1 surround sound) with the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=London_Metropolitan_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="London Metropolitan Orchestra (page does not exist)">London Metropolitan Orchestra</a> at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Narholz was signed when series music editor Nick Carr recommended him to Hillenburg after they worked together at the <a href="/wiki/APM_Music" title="APM Music">Associated Production Music</a> library.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OralHistory_10-7"><a href="#cite_note-OralHistory-10">[10]</a></sup> Narholz was honored at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">ASCAP Film and Television Music Awards</a> for his work on the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and received a nomination for <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award_for_Music_in_a_Feature_Production" title="Annie Award for Music in a Feature Production">Music in an Animated Feature Production</a> at the <a href="/wiki/32nd_Annie_Awards" title="32nd Annie Awards">32nd Annie Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnieMovie_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-AnnieMovie-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg"><img alt="Two guitarists (one singing) and a drummer onstage" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg/250px-The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg/375px-The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg/500px-The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Flaming_Lips_SoCo_Music_Experience_01-2007-09-08.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Flaming Lips recorded "SpongeBob &amp; Patrick Confront the Psychic Wall of Energy".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>American rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips" title="The Flaming Lips">The Flaming Lips</a> recorded "SpongeBob &amp; Patrick Confront the Psychic Wall of Energy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TFL1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-TFL1-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilcoLips_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-WilcoLips-54">[54]</a></sup> They shot the song's <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a>, directed by band member <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Coyne" title="Wayne Coyne">Wayne Coyne</a> and filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Beesley" title="Bradley Beesley">Bradley Beesley</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TFL1_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-TFL1-53">[53]</a></sup> Coyne said, "Stephen [Hillenburg] seems to be a fan of the weirder music of the late '80s and early '90s [...] He wanted to evoke the music he got turned onto back then."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TFL1_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-TFL1-53">[53]</a></sup> Coyne suggested a duet with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, but Hillenburg refused,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wierdo_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wierdo-55">[55]</a></sup> saying "I don't want any of those sort of commercial weirdos on there. I don't like those commercial people. I like you guys, and Wilco and <a href="/wiki/Ween" title="Ween">Ween</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wierdo_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wierdo-55">[55]</a></sup> American band <a href="/wiki/Wilco" title="Wilco">Wilco</a> wrote and recorded "Just a Kid".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilcoLips_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-WilcoLips-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilco_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilco-56">[56]</a></sup> One of the film's producers contacted frontman <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Tweedy" title="Jeff Tweedy">Jeff Tweedy</a> after seeing a SpongeBob <a href="/wiki/Air_freshener" title="Air freshener">air freshener</a> hanging from Tweedy's rearview mirror in <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Trying_to_Break_Your_Heart:_A_Film_About_Wilco" title="I Am Trying to Break Your Heart: A Film About Wilco">I Am Trying to Break Your Heart: A Film About Wilco</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilco_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wilco-56">[56]</a></sup> Tweedy said, "I fell in love with SpongeBob when I heard him describe the darkness at the bottom of the sea as 'advanced darkness' [...] How could I not write a song for this film? It automatically makes me the coolest dad on the block."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilco_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wilco-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Avril_Lavigne" title="Avril Lavigne">Avril Lavigne</a> recorded the series' theme for the soundtrack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Other artists contributing to the soundtrack were <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Motörhead">Motörhead</a>, singing "You Better Swim" (a derivative of their 1992 song "You'd Better Run");<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prince_Paul_(producer)" title="Prince Paul (producer)">Prince Paul</a> ("Prince Paul's Bubble Party");<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ween" title="Ween">Ween</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Ocean_Man" title="Ocean Man">Ocean Man</a>"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-60">[60]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Shins" title="The Shins">the Shins</a> ("They'll Soon Discover", partially written in 2001).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>"The Best Day Ever", written by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kenny" title="Tom Kenny">Tom Kenny</a> (SpongeBob's voice actor) and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Paley" title="Andy Paley">Andy Paley</a>, was featured in the film and on its soundtrack. Kenny and Paley were working on what would become the album <a href="/wiki/Best_Day_Ever#Album" title="Best Day Ever"><i>The Best Day Ever</i></a>, writing "The Best Day Ever" and "Under My Rock".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-64">[64]</a></sup> The film's production team needed two more tracks for the soundtrack;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-64">[64]</a></sup> Hillenburg heard the songs, and decided to include them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-64">[64]</a></sup> "The Best Day Ever" ended up being played during the film's <a href="/wiki/Closing_credits" title="Closing credits">closing credits</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deleted_scenes">Deleted scenes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Deleted scenes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpongeBob,_Patrick_and_Sandy_(animatic).jpg"><img alt="Sitting squirrel and pencil sketch" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="258" data-file-width="496" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/SpongeBob%2C_Patrick_and_Sandy_%28animatic%29.jpg/260px-SpongeBob%2C_Patrick_and_Sandy_%28animatic%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/SpongeBob%2C_Patrick_and_Sandy_%28animatic%29.jpg/390px-SpongeBob%2C_Patrick_and_Sandy_%28animatic%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f9/SpongeBob%2C_Patrick_and_Sandy_%28animatic%29.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpongeBob,_Patrick_and_Sandy_(animatic).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Animatic of deleted scene, with SpongeBob and Patrick (right) encountering Sandy Cheeks (left) on the surface</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The DVD and Blu-ray releases include <a href="/wiki/Storyboard#Animatics" title="Storyboard">animatics</a> of <a href="/wiki/Deleted_scene" title="Deleted scene">deleted scenes</a> from the film, including SpongeBob and Patrick's meeting with <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Cheeks" title="Sandy Cheeks">Sandy Cheeks</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrel</a>) on the surface after their escape from Shell City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> Patrick repeatedly <a href="/wiki/Vomiting" title="Vomiting">vomits</a>, upset by Sandy's unusual appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> The squirrel is pursued by black-suited <a href="/wiki/Pest_control" title="Pest control">exterminators</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> and defends herself with <a href="/wiki/Acorn" title="Acorn">acorns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> She informs SpongeBob and Patrick that they can return to Bikini Bottom by taking a bus at the beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-4"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>When SpongeBob awakens with a hangover on the Goofy Goober party boat, he asks a waiter for a "Double-Fudge Spinny";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-5"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> the rejected line was used in a <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie-in</a> book, <i>Ice-Cream Dreams</i>, which was based on the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeletedScenes_65-6"><a href="#cite_note-DeletedScenes-65">[65]</a></sup> In 2013 the film's lead storyboard artist, <a href="/wiki/Sherm_Cohen" title="Sherm Cohen">Sherm Cohen</a>, released a <a href="/wiki/Storyboard" title="Storyboard">storyboard panel</a> of a deleted scene from the film with SpongeBob awakening from his dream saying "WEEEEE!" and Mr. Krabs holding a manager's hat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg"><img alt="Large, Chinese-style building with people in front" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4928" data-file-width="3264" height="332" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg/220px-Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg/330px-Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg/440px-Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The film had its yellow-carpet world premiere at Grauman's Chinese Theatre in Hollywood on November 14, 2004.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film's <a href="/wiki/Trailer_(promotion)" title="Trailer (promotion)">trailer</a> was released on May 19, 2004, and was attached to <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">Shrek 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> opened in theaters on November 19, 2004;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Release_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Release-69">[69]</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/Red_carpet" title="Red carpet">yellow-carpet</a> world premiere was at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TCL_Chinese_Theatre" title="TCL Chinese Theatre">Grauman's Chinese Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> on November 14, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Among celebrities who saw the premiere with their children were <a href="/wiki/Ray_Romano" title="Ray Romano">Ray Romano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_Cube" title="Ice Cube">Ice Cube</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Crime_Scene_Investigation" title="CSI: Crime Scene Investigation">CSI: Crime Scene Investigation</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Gary_Dourdan" title="Gary Dourdan">Gary Dourdan</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Kudrow" title="Lisa Kudrow">Lisa Kudrow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-73">[73]</a></sup> The carpet was a disturbing reminder of home for <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kenny" title="Tom Kenny">Tom Kenny</a>, SpongeBob's voice actor; he said, "I have a 15-month-old daughter, so I'm no stranger to yellow carpets."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-WP-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Julia Pistor, the film's co-producer, said that although Nickelodeon (which owns the <i>SpongeBob</i> trademark) wanted to sell character-themed <a href="/wiki/Backpack" title="Backpack">backpacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lunch_box" title="Lunch box">lunch boxes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watch" title="Watch">wristwatches</a> it respected Hillenburg's integrity and gave him control of merchandising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> Hillenburg had no problem with candy and ice cream <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie-ins</a>, Pistor said (because of the treats' simplicity),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> but he had issues with <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_restaurant" title="Fast food restaurant">fast food tie-ins</a>; according to him, the latter was "full of hidden additives."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> Pistor said, "The trouble is that you can't go out with animated films without a fast-food tie-in [...] People don't take you seriously."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-7"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup> Hillenburg replied, "Yeah, well, my take on that is that we shouldn't do that [...] We didn't want to suddenly become the people serving up food that's not that good for you - especially kids. We work with <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>, and they make toys and watches. But to actually take the step of pushing the food, that's crossing the line. I don't want to be the Pied Piper of fast food."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel2_8-8"><a href="#cite_note-Edel2-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film was promoted across the United States. Nickelodeon joined <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> for a 12-figure <a href="/wiki/Toy" title="Toy">toy</a> line based on the film, and about 4,700 Burger King stores perched 9-foot (2.7 m), inflatable SpongeBob figures on their roofs as part of the promotion (one of the largest in <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_restaurant" title="Fast food restaurant">fast-food</a> history).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup> Customers could also purchase one of five different SpongeBob-themed watches for $1.99 with the purchase of a value meal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 11, 2004, it was reported that a number of the inflatables had been stolen from Burger King roofs nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribune_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribune-75">[75]</a></sup> Burger King chief marketing officer Russ Klein said, "As to the motives behind these apparent 'spongenappings', we can only speculate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWN_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-76">[76]</a></sup> We did receive one ransom note related to an inflatable SpongeBob disappearance in <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWN_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-76">[76]</a></sup> The chain offered a year's supply of <a href="/wiki/Whopper" title="Whopper">Whopper</a> sandwiches as a reward for information leading to the return of inflatables stolen in November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press1_74-5"><a href="#cite_note-Press1-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWN_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> One was found attached to a railing at the football-field 50-yard line at an <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a> college,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CelebrityCafe_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-CelebrityCafe-79">[79]</a></sup> and another under a bed in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CelebrityCafe_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-CelebrityCafe-79">[79]</a></sup> A ransom note was found for a third: "We have SpongeBob. Give us 10 Krabby Patties, fries, and milkshakes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CelebrityCafe_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-CelebrityCafe-79">[79]</a></sup> Steven Simon and Conrad (C.J.) Mercure Jr. were arrested after stealing an inflatable from a Burger King in <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_County,_Maryland" title="St. Mary's County, Maryland">St. Mary's County, Maryland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TST_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-TST-81">[81]</a></sup> While facing up to 18 months in jail and a $500 fine, Simon and Mercure said they were proud of what they did;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TST_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-TST-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPost2_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPost2-82">[82]</a></sup> Simon said, "Once we got caught by the police, we were like, now we can tell everybody."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TST_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-TST-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPost2_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-WPost2-82">[82]</a></sup> The following year Burger King took "extra security precautions", when <a href="/wiki/Stormtrooper_(Star_Wars)" title="Stormtrooper (Star Wars)">Stormtroopers</a> from <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> guarded the delivery of <i>Star Wars</i> toys to a Burger King in <a href="/wiki/North_Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="North Hollywood, Los Angeles">North Hollywood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> in the western <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, joined with Nickelodeon to create the first Cayman Islands Sea School with SpongeBob for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cayman_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cayman-84">[84]</a></sup> The partnership was announced by Pilar Bush, Deputy Director of Tourism for Cayman Islands, on March 10, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cayman_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cayman-84">[84]</a></sup> As part of the agreement the Cayman partnership was seen on Nickelodeon's global multimedia platforms, including on-air, online and in magazines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cayman_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cayman-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Nickelodeon and <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Schuster" title="Simon &amp; Schuster">Simon Spotlight</a> released a book, <i>Ice-Cream Dreams</i>, as a tie-in to the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> It was written by Nancy E. Krulik and illustrated by Heather Martinez, with Krulik and <a href="/wiki/Derek_Drymon" title="Derek Drymon">Derek Drymon</a> as contributors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie_300"><i>SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> 300</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: SpongeBob SquarePants Movie 300">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 15, 2004, the film was the first to sponsor a <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> race: the 300-mile (480 km), <a href="/wiki/2004_NASCAR_Busch_Series" title="2004 NASCAR Busch Series">Busch Series</a> <i>SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> 300 at <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRNews_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRNews-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlotte_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charlotte-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> It was the first race of its kind where children at the track could listen to a special, "kid-friendly" radio broadcast of the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRNews_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-PRNews-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlotte_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Charlotte-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kyle_Busch" title="Kyle Busch">Kyle Busch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Johnson" title="Jimmie Johnson">Jimmie Johnson</a> debuted a pair of <i>SpongeBob SquarePants</i>-themed <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a> <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> race cars in the race. Johnson's No. 48 Chevrolet included an image of SpongeBob across the hood, and Busch's No. 5 Chevrolet featured Patrick Star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRNews_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-PRNews-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlotte_92-2"><a href="#cite_note-Charlotte-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Johnson said, "This sounds so cool [...] I know there are a lot of families who will be excited that Lowe's is doing this. The great thing is there will be something for every type of race fan. Plus how can we go wrong with SpongeBob helping us out on the car?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRNews_89-3"><a href="#cite_note-PRNews-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlotte_92-3"><a href="#cite_note-Charlotte-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="DVD"></span><span id="Video"></span> The film was released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> on March 1, 2005, in <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)" title="Aspect ratio (image)">wide- and full-screen</a> editions, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paramount_Home_Entertainment" title="Paramount Home Entertainment">Paramount Home Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lecter_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lecter-95">[95]</a></sup> It contains an 18-minute featurette, <i>The Absorbing Tale Behind The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i>, featuring interviews with most of the principal cast and crew; a 15-minute featurette, <i>Case of the Sponge "Bob"</i>, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Michel_Cousteau" title="Jean-Michel Cousteau">Jean-Michel Cousteau</a>; a 20-minute <a href="/wiki/Storyboard#Animatics" title="Storyboard">animatic segment</a> featuring scenes from the film with dialogue by the original artists, and the film's trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lecter_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lecter-95">[95]</a></sup> The film was released as a <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a>-plus-DVD combination pack on March 29, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> version was released on March 1, 2005; it was the final VHS animated film from Nickelodeon Movies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> As a tie-in to the film's DVD release, <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> served a limited-edition Under-the-Sea Pineapple <a href="/wiki/Slurpee" title="Slurpee">Slurpee</a> in March 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was re-released on Blu-ray on December 30, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> earned $9,559,752 on its opening day in the United States, second behind <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/National_Treasure_(film)" title="National Treasure (film)">National Treasure</a></i> (which earned $11 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> It grossed a combined total of $32,018,216 during its opening weekend, on 4,300 screens at 3,212 theaters, averaging $9,968 per venue (or $7,446 per screen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OW_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-OW-104">[104]</a></sup> again second to <i>National Treasure</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OW_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-OW-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The film dropped an unexpected 44 percent over the Thanksgiving weekend, and 57 percent the weekend after that.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weekends_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weekends-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The opening weekend earned 37.48 percent of the film's final gross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weekends_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weekends-108">[108]</a></sup> It closed on March 24, 2005, failing to out-gross holiday animated competitors <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredibles" title="The Incredibles">The Incredibles</a></i> (from Disney-<a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>, grossing $261,441,092) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Polar_Express_(film)" title="The Polar Express (film)">The Polar Express</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a>, grossing $183,373,735). It was still profitable for distributor <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> and producer <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Movies" title="Nickelodeon Movies">Nickelodeon Movies</a>, earning $85,417,988 in the United States and $140,161,792 worldwide on a budget of $30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3">[3]</a></sup> The film was the 29th-highest-grossing 2004 film domestically<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> and is the sixth-highest-grossing animated TV adaptation of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Reviews"></span><span id="Critics"></span> On <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, the film holds a rating of 68%, based on 125 reviews, with an average score of 6.2/10. The site's consensus reads, "Surreally goofy and entertaining for both children and their parents."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cream_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-cream-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gave the film a score of 66 out of 100, based on 32 critics, indicating "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a>, audiences gave the film a grade of "B+" on an A+ to F scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:27%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>All of this happens in jolly animation with bright colors and is ever so much more entertaining than you are probably imagining. No doubt right now you're asking yourself why you have read this far in the review, given the near-certainty that you will not be going anywhere near a <i>SpongeBob SquarePants</i> movie, unless you are the parent or adult guardian of a <i>SpongeBob SquarePants</i> fan, in which case your fate is sealed. Assuming that few members of SpongeBob's primary audience are reading this (or can read), all I can tell you is, the movie is likely to be more fun than you expect.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>, in his review for the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebert_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-116">[116]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> gave the film three out of four stars, calling it "the 'Good Burger' of animation ... plopping us down inside a fast-food war being fought by sponges, starfish, crabs, tiny plankton and mighty King Neptune."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebert_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-116">[116]</a></sup> Ed Park of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> wrote, "No <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>? No problem! An unstoppable good-mood generator, the resolutely 2-D [<i>The</i>] <i>SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> has more yuks than <i><a href="/wiki/Shark_Tale" title="Shark Tale">Shark Tale</a></i> and enough soul to swallow <i><a href="/wiki/The_Polar_Express_(film)" title="The Polar Express (film)">The Polar Express</a></i> whole."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Michael Rechtshaffen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> gave the film a positive review, calling it "an animated adventure that's funnier than <i>Shark Tale</i> and more charming than <i>The Polar Express</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Randy Cordova of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arizona_Republic" title="The Arizona Republic">The Arizona Republic</a></i> said, "Like the <a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants" title="SpongeBob SquarePants">TV show it's based on</a>, it's a daffy, enjoyable creation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jami_Bernard" title="Jami Bernard">Jami Bernard</a> of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i> gave the feature a score of three out of four: "It's not <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredibles" title="The Incredibles">The Incredibles</a></i>, or one of those animated features that spent zillions on character design, pedigree and verisimilitude. But SpongeBob is a sweet, silly thing with a child-friendly esthetic all its own."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Will Lawrence of <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> gave the film four out of five stars, calling it "a film for kids, students, stoners, anyone who enjoys a break from reality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Schwarzbaum" title="Lisa Schwarzbaum">Lisa Schwarzbaum</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> gave it a B-minus grade: "The best moments in his [SpongeBob SquarePants] first movie outing are those that feel most TV-like, just another day in the eternally optimistic undersea society created with such contagious silliness by Stephen Hillenburg."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Desson_Thomson" title="Desson Thomson">Desson Thomson</a> of <i>The Washington Post</i> enjoyed the film: "You gotta love SpongeBob. Coolest sponge in the sea, although this one has a suspiciously manufactured look."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carla Meyer of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> wrote that "<i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> retains the 2-D charm of the hugely popular <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> cartoon but adds a few tricks – a little 3-D here, a little <a href="/wiki/David_Hasselhoff" title="David Hasselhoff">David Hasselhoff</a> there. The series' appeal never lay in its visuals, however. 'SpongeBob' endeared itself to kids and adults through sweetness and cleverness, also abundant here."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> gave it a score of four out of five: "If you're tired of ... bluster and swagger, SpongeBob is your man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Tom Maurstad of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dallas_Morning_News" title="The Dallas Morning News">The Dallas Morning News</a></i> also gave the film a B-minus grade: "Being so good is what led to making the movie, and it's also the reason that many small-screen episodes are better than this big-screen venture."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some reviews praised David Hasselhoff's appearance in the film. Jennifer Frey of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> wrote, "Getting to see the hairs on Hasselhoff's back (and thighs, and calves) magnified exponentially is perhaps a bit creepy. Like the movie, it's all in good fun."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Nancy Basile of <a href="/wiki/About.com" title="About.com">About.com</a>, who gave the film four out of five stars, wrote that Hasselhoff "must have a great sense of humor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Cinema Blend founder Joshua Tyler called Hasselhoff's role "the best movie cameo I've seen since <a href="/wiki/Fred_Savage" title="Fred Savage">Fred Savage</a> stuck a joint in his crotch and played a clarinet to charm the resulting smoke like a snake."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:35%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>There's plenty to treasure in <i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i>, but for all the spit-and-polish animation and the rollicking soundtrack (which includes an original song by <a href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips" title="The Flaming Lips">the Flaming Lips</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Ween" title="Ween">Ween</a>'s gorgeous "Ocean Man," from their <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mollusk" title="The Mollusk">Mollusk</a></i> album), this isn't the yellow one's most thrilling hour—or 80 minutes."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">David Edelstein, in his <i>Slate</i> review<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slate-130">[130]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Edelstein" title="David Edelstein">David Edelstein</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> criticized the film's plot, calling it a "big, heavy anchor of a story structure to weigh him down."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Slate-130">[130]</a></sup> Mike Clark of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> called it "harmlessly off-the-cuff — but facing far more pedigreed multiplex competition ... SpongeBob barely rates as OK when compared with <i>The Incredibles</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> A reviewer noted in <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Out_(magazine)" title="Time Out (magazine)">Time Out London</a></i>, "Anyone expecting anything more risky will be sadly disappointed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> In his <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> review, <a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> said the film "takes on rather too much water during its extended feature-length submersion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_Movie_Database" title="Internet Movie Database">Internet Movie Database</a> staff member David N. Butterworth gave it zero stars, saying that "For much like fish, <i>The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</i> truly stinks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the film was generally well received by fans of the show, it is considered a turning point in the show's history; many fans believe that the television series has <a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants#Criticism_of_declining_quality_and_2012_ratings_slide" title="SpongeBob SquarePants">declined in quality</a> since the film's release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSN_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSN-135">[135]</a></sup> While episodes aired before the film were praised for their "uncanny brilliance",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> those aired after the film have been called "kid-pandering attention-waster[s]",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> "tedious",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> "boring", "dreck",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> a "depressing plateau of mediocrity"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> and "laugh-skimpy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mavis_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mavis-141">[141]</a></sup> After the film's release, fans "began to turn away from the show," causing <a href="/wiki/Fansite" title="Fansite">fansites</a> to "bec[ome] deserted."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSN_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-MSN-135">[135]</a></sup> Some fans believe that the show's 2012 ratings decline correlates with a decline in quality, and "whatever fan support [the show] enjoys is not enough" to save it from its slide in ratings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSN_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-MSN-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hillenburg.jpg"><img alt="Smiling man in gray jacket" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="312" data-file-width="248" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Stephen_Hillenburg.jpg/200px-Stephen_Hillenburg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Stephen_Hillenburg.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hillenburg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Director <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hillenburg" title="Stephen Hillenburg">Stephen Hillenburg</a> was nominated at the <a href="/wiki/32nd_Annie_Awards" title="32nd Annie Awards">32nd Annie Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award_for_Directing_in_a_Feature_Production" title="Annie Award for Directing in a Feature Production">Directing an Animated Feature Production</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnnieMovie_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-AnnieMovie-51">[51]</a></sup></div>
